  ---
  The Audio Pipeline: What Working Code Looks Like vs Ours

  Here's the key insight: Pipecat's implementation is the closest to what we need because it's literally built for
  Gemini Live WebSocket. Let me map it side-by-side with our code.

  The Central Truth: Audio Format

  Pipecat (AudioCommon.swift:5-7):
  static var serverAudioFormat: AVAudioFormat = {
      AVAudioFormat(commonFormat: .pcmFormatInt16, sampleRate: 24000, channels: 1, interleaved: false)!
  }()

  Wait — this is interesting. Pipecat uses 24kHz for BOTH directions (send AND receive). But Gemini's docs say input is
  16kHz and output is 24kHz. Let me check what swift-gemini-api does...

  From the swift-gemini-api research:
  - Capture target: 16kHz (getDestFormat() returns 16000)
  - Playback: 24kHz (sampleRate: Double = 24000)
  - MIME type: "audio/pcm;rate=16000" for sending

  So there's a discrepancy:

  ┌───────────────┬──────────────────────┬─────────────────┬──────────────────────┐
  │               │   swift-gemini-api   │     Pipecat     │       Our code       │
  ├───────────────┼──────────────────────┼─────────────────┼──────────────────────┤
  │ Capture rate  │ 16kHz                │ 24kHz           │ Device native (BUG)  │
  ├───────────────┼──────────────────────┼─────────────────┼──────────────────────┤
  │ Playback rate │ 24kHz                │ 24kHz           │ 16kHz (BUG)          │
  ├───────────────┼──────────────────────┼─────────────────┼──────────────────────┤
  │ Send MIME     │ audio/pcm;rate=16000 │ (need to check) │ audio/pcm;rate=16000 │
  └───────────────┴──────────────────────┴─────────────────┴──────────────────────┘

  Both reference implementations confirm: playback must be 24kHz. For capture, both 16kHz and 24kHz work — Gemini
  accepts both, but 16kHz is more bandwidth-efficient.

  Capture: Three Approaches Compared

  Our code (broken — ChatViewModel.swift:435-491):
  // Gets device native rate (48kHz), no resampling
  let format = inputNode.outputFormat(forBus: 0)
  inputNode.installTap(onBus: 0, bufferSize: 1024, format: format) { buffer, _ in
      self?.processAudioBuffer(buffer)  // Just clips float→Int16, no resample
  }

  Pipecat (working — AudioRecorder.swift:17-75):
  audioEngine = AVAudioEngine()
  try audioEngine.inputNode.setVoiceProcessingEnabled(true)  // KEY: echo cancellation!
  let inputFormat = inputNode.inputFormat(forBus: 0)          // Note: inputFormat, not outputFormat

  let formatConverter = AVAudioConverter(from: inputFormat, to: AudioCommon.serverAudioFormat)!

  audioEngine.inputNode.installTap(
      onBus: 0,
      bufferSize: UInt32(AudioCommon.serverAudioFormat.sampleRate) / UInt32(AudioCommon.audioLevelReportingRate),
      format: inputFormat
  ) { inputBuffer, time in
      // 1. Audio level for UI
      var audioLevel = AudioCommon.calculateRMSAudioLevel(fromBuffer: inputBuffer)
      audioLevel = min(1, audioLevel * 10)

      // 2. Resample using AVAudioConverter
      let targetBuffer = Self.convertToTargetFormat(inputBuffer: inputBuffer, ...)

      // 3. Extract raw Int16 bytes
      let channels = UnsafeBufferPointer(start: targetBuffer.int16ChannelData, count: 1)
      let data = NSData(bytes: channels[0], length: Int(targetBuffer.frameLength * bytesPerFrame))

      // 4. Yield to async stream
      streamAudioContinuation?.yield(data as Data)
  }

  swift-gemini-api (working — uses lower-level AudioUnit):
  // Uses AudioUnit (RemoteIO) instead of AVAudioEngine
  // AudioConverterFillComplexBuffer for resampling to 16kHz
  // Base64 encodes directly in the callback
  // Calls onChunk(base64String) callback

  Three critical things Pipecat does that we don't:
  1. setVoiceProcessingEnabled(true) — This enables echo cancellation so the mic doesn't pick up the AI's audio from the
   speaker. Without this, the AI hears itself and creates a feedback loop.
  2. AVAudioConverter — Properly resamples from device native rate to target rate.
  3. Uses inputFormat not outputFormat — There's a known iOS bug where outputFormat reports 0Hz after reconnection.
  Using inputFormat(forBus: 0) is more reliable.

  Playback: Pipecat's Pattern

  Our code (broken — ChatViewModel.swift:495-571):
  // Format is wrong (16kHz instead of 24kHz)
  let format = AVAudioFormat(commonFormat: .pcmFormatInt16, sampleRate: 16_000, channels: 1, interleaved: false)
  // Directly schedules Int16 buffers

  Pipecat (AudioPlayer.swift:15-111):
  // Input format: server's Int16 at 24kHz
  inputAudioFormat = AudioCommon.serverAudioFormat  // Int16, 24kHz, mono

  // Player format: Float32 at 24kHz (AVAudioEngine prefers float)
  playerAudioFormat = AVAudioFormat(
      standardFormatWithSampleRate: inputAudioFormat.sampleRate,
      channels: inputAudioFormat.channelCount
  )!  // standardFormat = Float32

  // Converter from Int16 → Float32 (same rate, just format change)
  inputToPlayerAudioConverter = AVAudioConverter(from: inputAudioFormat, to: playerAudioFormat)!

  func enqueueBytes(_ bytes: Data) {
      // 1. Create Int16 buffer from raw bytes
      let inputBuffer = AVAudioPCMBuffer(pcmFormat: inputAudioFormat, frameCapacity: ...)!
      inputBuffer.frameLength = inputBuffer.frameCapacity
      (bytes as NSData).getBytes(UnsafeMutableRawPointer(channels[0]), length: bytes.count)

      // 2. Convert Int16 → Float32 for AVAudioEngine
      let playerBuffer = AVAudioPCMBuffer(pcmFormat: playerAudioFormat, frameCapacity: ...)!
      try! inputToPlayerAudioConverter.convert(to: playerBuffer, from: inputBuffer)

      // 3. Schedule with completion tracking
      playerNode.scheduleBuffer(playerBuffer, completionCallbackType: .dataPlayedBack) { ... }
  }

  Key insight: AVAudioEngine's mainMixerNode doesn't support Int16 directly (see Pipecat's comment on line 35-36:
  "doesn't seem to support pcm 16 here"). So they convert Int16→Float32 at the same sample rate (24kHz), then schedule
  the Float32 buffer. Our code tries to schedule Int16 directly, which may silently fail on some devices.

  Mute: Simple and Correct

  swift-gemini-api:
  public func sendAudio(base64: String) {
      if mute { return }  // Just don't send
      // ...
  }

  Our code stops/starts the entire AVAudioEngine, which is expensive (~50-100ms gap) and can cause audio route changes.
  The flag-based approach is instant.

  Device Change Handling

  Pipecat (AudioRecorder.swift:98-104 and AudioPlayer.swift:64-68):
  func adaptToDeviceChange() throws {
      let wasRunning = audioEngine.isRunning
      stop()
      if wasRunning {
          try resume()
      }
  }

  Both recorder and player have this method. When a Bluetooth device connects/disconnects, they completely tear down and
   rebuild the engine. Our code doesn't handle this at all — the handleRouteChange notification only updates UI state.

  The "isSpeaking" Detection

  Pipecat tracks enqueuedBufferCount:
  private func incrementEnqueuedBufferCount() {
      enqueuedBufferCount += 1
      if enqueuedBufferCount == 1 {
          delegate?.audioPlayerDidStartPlayback(self)  // AI started speaking
      }
  }
  private func decrementEnqueuedBufferCount() {
      enqueuedBufferCount -= 1
      if enqueuedBufferCount == 0 {
          delegate?.audioPlayerDidFinishPlayback(self)  // AI finished speaking
      }
  }

  Our code uses callState.isSpeaking which is set in playNextAudioChunk() — similar concept but less precise.

  ---
  Summary: What We Need to Change

  ┌────────────────────┬───────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────┐
  │       Issue        │        Current        │               Fix               │            Reference             │
  ├────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Echo cancellation  │ None                  │ setVoiceProcessingEnabled(true) │ Pipecat line 26                  │
  ├────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Input format       │ outputFormat          │ inputFormat(forBus: 0)          │ Pipecat line 30                  │
  ├────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Capture resampling │ None (sends at 48kHz) │ AVAudioConverter to 16kHz       │ Pipecat lines 33-55              │
  ├────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Playback rate      │ 16kHz                 │ 24kHz                           │ Pipecat AudioCommon.swift:6      │
  ├────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Playback format    │ Int16 direct          │ Int16→Float32 via converter     │ Pipecat AudioPlayer.swift:97-102 │
  ├────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Mute               │ Engine stop/start     │ Flag-based skip                 │ swift-gemini-api                 │
  ├────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Device changes     │ UI update only        │ Teardown + rebuild engine       │ Pipecat line 98-104              │
  ├────────────────────┼───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Buffer size        │ 1024 fixed            │ sampleRate / reportingRate      │ Pipecat line 39                  │
  └────────────────────┴───────────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────┘

  The Pipecat implementation is essentially a drop-in pattern for our use case — same WebSocket target (Gemini), same
  audio requirements. Want to proceed with translating these patterns into our ChatViewModel.swift, or dig deeper into
  any specific part first?

> hey claude i'd like to rebuild the chatscreen module. i did some research for the ui and the infrastructure. the
  goal is to reach imessage/facetime parity with gemini live API. right now we have a text model and we also have a
   audio model and i think that is a decent paradigm that we likely will keep. ill give you some repositories you
  might want to clone for reference.

  ### 1. The Real-Time Connection (Gemini Live API)

  You need a WebSocket client that can stream 16kHz PCM audio up to the model and handle 24kHz audio coming back,
  alongside tool-calling events.

  **Relevant Repositories:**

  * **[`paradigms-of-intelligence/swift-gemini-api`](https://www.google.com/search?q=%5Bhttps://github.com/paradigm
  s-of-intelligence/swift-gemini-api%5D(https://github.com/paradigms-of-intelligence/swift-gemini-api)):** This is
  the current go-to Swift package for this exact use case. It includes a `GeminiLiveClient` that handles the
  bidirectional WebSocket streaming, Voice Activity Detection (VAD), and raw audio formatting out of the box.
  * **[`pipecat-ai/pipecat-client-ios-gemini-live-websocket`](https://www.google.com/search?q=%5Bhttps://github.com
  /pipecat-ai/pipecat-client-ios-gemini-live-websocket%5D(https://github.com/pipecat-ai/pipecat-client-ios-gemini-l
  ive-websocket)):** If you plan on building a more complex agentic workflow later (like piping the audio through
  other services before it hits Gemini), Pipecat’s iOS SDK has a dedicated transport layer specifically for the
  Gemini Live WebSocket.

  **Implementation Logic:**
  Initialize the client, pass your API key, and set up the callbacks for `onAudioReceived`. You will feed the
  microphone buffers directly into their `sendAudio(data:)` function.

  ### 2. Audio Routing & Mute (AVAudioSession)

  To get that native "phone call" feel with the speakerphone and mute buttons, you have to bypass SwiftUI entirely
  and manipulate Apple's underlying `AVAudioSession`.

  **Implementation Logic:**
  You don't need a heavy library for this; it's just a few lines of native AVFoundation code.

  * **Setup:** Configure the session for a two-way voice chat.
  ```swift
  let session = AVAudioSession.sharedInstance()
  try session.setCategory(.playAndRecord, mode: .voiceChat, options: [.defaultToSpeaker, .allowBluetooth])
  try session.setActive(true)

  ```


  * **The Speakerphone Button:** Bind your SwiftUI UI to toggle the audio port override.
  ```swift
  // Turn ON Speakerphone
  try session.overrideOutputAudioPort(.speaker)
  // Turn OFF Speakerphone (Routes to earpiece)
  try session.overrideOutputAudioPort(.none)

  ```


  * **The Mute Button:** If you are using the `swift-gemini-api` package, simply wrap the `sendAudio` call in a
  guard statement (`guard !isMuted else { return }`). This drops the packets locally, saving bandwidth while
  ensuring Gemini hears dead silence.

  let start by establishing exactly what imessage/facetime(whether on video mode or just calling) look like ui
  wise. and then once we have all of that established, the buttons and styling, we will fill in the information
  transfer to gemini api

       ---
       3. Audio/Voice Call Implementation

       Voice Call Architecture:

       Call State Management (in ChatViewModel):
       struct CallSessionState {
         var isPresented = false        // Call UI shown?
         var isListening = false         // Microphone active?
         var isSpeaking = false          // AI speaking?
         var audioLevel: Float           // Real-time audio level (0-1)
         var isVideoStreaming = false    // Video mode active?
         var videoFrameInterval: TimeInterval = 0.2
       }

       Audio Pipeline (ChatViewModel):

       1. Audio Capture (startAudioCapture):
         - Uses AVAudioEngine with input node tap
         - Configures AVAudioSession: .playAndRecord, .voiceChat mode
         - Buffer size: 1024 frames
         - Processes audio buffer → calculates audio level → converts to PCM16 → sends to Gemini
       2. Audio Playback (playAudio):
         - Separate AVAudioEngine for playback
         - Uses AVAudioPlayerNode
         - Converts incoming Data → PCM16 buffer → queues for playback
         - Handles sequential chunk playback with completion handlers
       3. Audio Format: PCM 16-bit, 16kHz, mono
         - Conversion: convertToPCM16() via float → Int16 conversion
       4. CallKit Integration (CallKitManager.swift):
         - Registers system call through CXProvider
         - Integrates with iOS system call UI
         - Callbacks: onStartAudio, onStopAudio, onMuteChanged
         - Handles mute state sync: toggleMute() → stops/starts capture
       5. Dual-Mode Approach:
         - CallKit Enabled (preferred): Delegates audio setup to CallKit manager
         - Fallback Mode: Direct AVAudioSession setup without CallKit
         - Handles audio interruptions (phone calls, alarms)

       Call Lifecycle:
       - startVoiceSession(): Presents call UI, connects WebSocket (audio mode), starts capture if CallKit allows
       - stopVoiceSession(): Dismisses UI, stops capture, stops playback, disconnects WebSocket
       - connect(mode: .audio): Initiates WebSocket connection to Gemini Live API
       - disconnect(): Closes WebSocket, cancels all pending tasks

       Call Presentation Styles (CallPresentationStyle):
       - fullScreen: Dedicated call interface
       - translucentOverlay: Call UI on top of chat (40% modal)
       - pictureInPicture: Draggable minimized call window

       Live Activity Integration (LiveActivityManager):
       - Displays call status in Dynamic Island
       - Updates duration in real-time
       - Shows connection state

       ---
       4. Gemini API Integration & WebSocket Implementation

       GeminiService.swift (60.8KB) - Comprehensive integration:

       Two-Mode Architecture:

       1. WebSocket (Audio Mode) - for live voice calls
         - URL: wss://generativelanguage.googleapis.com/ws/google.ai.generativelanguage.v1beta.GenerativeService.Bi
       diGenerateContent
         - Model: gemini-2.5-flash-native-audio-preview-12-2025
         - Bidirectional streaming: sends audio, receives audio + text + transcripts
       2. REST API (Text Mode) - for text/image messages
         - URL: https://generativelanguage.googleapis.com/v1beta/models/{model}:generateContent
         - Model: gemini-2.5-flash
         - Stateless requests with conversation history

       WebSocket Message Flow:

       Setup Phase:
       {
         "setup": {
           "model": "models/gemini-2.5-flash-native-audio-preview-12-2025",
           "generation_config": {
             "response_modalities": ["AUDIO"],
             "speech_config": { "voice_config": { "prebuilt_voice_config": { "voice_name": "Aoede" } } }
           },
           "system_instruction": { "parts": [{ "text": "system prompt" }] },
           "tools": [{ "function_declarations": [...] }],
           "output_audio_transcription": {}
         }
       }

       Server Response Messages:
       - setupComplete: Connection established
       - serverContent: Contains inputTranscript (user speech-to-text), modelTurn with parts
         - Parts can contain: text, inlineData (audio), transcript (AI output speech)
         - turnComplete flag indicates response finished
       - toolCall: Function calls from AI
         - Contains: functionCalls array with id, name, args

       Audio Streaming (during call):
       {
         "realtime_input": {
           "media_chunks": [{ "mime_type": "audio/pcm;rate=16000", "data": "base64-encoded-pcm" }]
         }
       }

       Text Sending (can use WebSocket if connected, else REST):
       {
         "client_content": {
           "turns": [{
             "role": "user",
             "parts": [{ "text": "message" }, { "inline_data": {...} }]
           }],
           "turn_complete": true
         }
       }

       Connection State Management:
       - connectionState enum: .disconnected, .connecting, .connected, .error(String)
       - Acceptance timeout: 6 seconds (must receive initial content)
       - Stream heartbeat timeout: 20 seconds (abort if no chunks)
       - Request timeout: 30 seconds
       - Tracks pendingMessageID with timeout handling

       Function Calling Integration:
       - Receives function calls from Gemini
       - Delegates to ChatViewModel.executeFunction() which routes to inventory/recipe handlers
       - Sends results back via sendFunctionResponse()
       - Tool call chips show pending → success/error status

       REST Conversation History:
       - Maintains stateful conversation context for text mode
       - Stores conversationHistory: [[String: Any]] with 20-turn cap
       - Auto-trims when exceeding limit
       - Includes user messages, assistant responses, and function results

       Delegate Protocol (GeminiServiceDelegate):
       // Connection
       func geminiServiceDidConnect(_ service: GeminiService)
       func geminiServiceDidDisconnect(_ service: GeminiService)
       func geminiService(_ service: GeminiService, didReceiveError error: Error)

       // Streaming
       func geminiService(_ service: GeminiService, didReceiveResponse text: String)
       func geminiService(_ service: GeminiService, didReceiveAudio data: Data)
       func geminiServiceDidStartResponse(_ service: GeminiService)
       func geminiServiceDidEndResponse(_ service: GeminiService)

       // Transcripts
       func geminiService(_ service: GeminiService, didReceiveTranscript transcript: String, isFinal: Bool)  // AI
       output
       func geminiService(_ service: GeminiService, didReceiveInputTranscript transcript: String, isFinal: Bool)
       // User input

       // Tool calling
       func geminiService(_ service: GeminiService, didStartFunctionCall id: String, name: String)
       func geminiService(_ service: GeminiService, didExecuteFunctionCall name: String, result: FunctionResult)

       ---
       5. Text vs. Audio Model Paradigm

       Current Architecture:

       SessionConfig Model Selection:
       enum SessionMode { case text, case audio }

       struct SessionConfig {
         let mode: SessionMode
         let model: String

         static let liveAudioModel = "gemini-2.5-flash-native-audio-preview-12-2025"
         static let defaultTextModel = "gemini-2.5-flash"

         static func text(model: String = defaultTextModel) -> SessionConfig
         static func audio(model: String = liveAudioModel) -> SessionConfig
       }

       How Model Selection Works:

       1. Text Messages:
         - Trigger: sendMessage(text:attachment:) during no active call
         - Route: REST API directly
         - Model: gemini-2.5-flash (standard text model)
         - Execution: sendTextREST(), sendPhotoREST(), sendTextWithPhotoREST()
         - Response handling: Single round-trip
       2. Audio/Voice Calls:
         - Trigger: startVoiceSession() → WebSocket connection
         - Route: WebSocket (persistent connection)
         - Model: gemini-2.5-flash-native-audio-preview-12-2025 (audio-optimized)
         - Execution: Continuous audio streaming via sendAudio(data:)
         - Response handling: Streaming responses (text + audio + transcripts)
       3. Hybrid Behavior (during voice call):
         - Text/images sent during call route via WebSocket (if connected)
         - Queued in pendingMessages if WebSocket not ready
         - Flushed when connection established

       System Prompt (single shared prompt in both modes):
       - Defined in GeminiService.sendSetupMessage()
       - Injected in REST requests and WebSocket setup
       - Chef persona: "Heard, Chef!" - warm, practical sous chef
       - Tool definitions auto-included
       - Guides model on tone, quantity acceptance, error handling

       Note on Models:
       - No local model fallback currently (stubbed in docs)
       - Both models support tool/function calling
       - Audio model can output both audio and text (configurable)
       - Voice config uses "Aoede" voice (5 prebuilt options available)

       ---
       6. Design Patterns, Navigation, Theming & Architecture

       MVVM with Service Layer:

       Views (SwiftUI) → ViewModels (@ObservableObject) → Services → Models (SwiftData)

       ChatView
         ↓
       ChatViewModel (state, business logic)
         ↓
       GeminiService (WebSocket/REST)
         ↓
       SwiftData (persistence)

       Key Design Patterns:

       1. State Management:
         - @Published for reactive properties in ChatViewModel
         - @State in Views for local UI state
         - @Environment for dependency injection (modelContext)
         - @ObservedObject for viewing published objects
       2. Async/Await & Task Management:
         - Tasks for long-running operations (network, audio processing)
         - MainActor constraint for UI updates
         - Cancellation handling via timeoutTask, restTask, heartbeatTask
         - Debouncing: scheduleTranscriptFinalize() with DispatchWorkItem
       3. Delegation Pattern:
         - GeminiServiceDelegate protocol for event callbacks
         - ChatViewModel implements delegate to receive connection/message events
         - CallKitManager closures: onStartAudio, onStopAudio, onMuteChanged
       4. Factory Pattern:
         - ChatAttachmentService.loadFromDocument(), loadFromCameraImage(), etc.
         - SessionConfig.text(), SessionConfig.audio()
       5. Repository Pattern:
         - SwiftData FetchDescriptor for querying messages/threads
         - loadOrCreateThread() logic in ChatViewModel
         - Conversation history management in GeminiService

       Navigation Architecture:

       MainTabView (4 tabs)
       ├── Tab 0: ChatView (with NavigationStack)
       │   ├── ChatThreadView (message list)
       │   ├── ChatInputBar
       │   └── CallView (full-screen modal)
       ├── Tab 1: InventoryView
       ├── Tab 2: RecipesView
       └── Tab 3: SettingsView

       Navigation Methods:
       - TabView for main tab switching
       - NavigationStack for future deep linking
       - .fullScreenCover() for CallView modal
       - .sheet() for attachment pickers, settings
       - .confirmationDialog() for attachment menu

       Call Presentation Transitions:
       - State variable callPresentationStyle: CallPresentationStyle
       - .transition(.opacity) for smooth appearance
       - Binding to track fullScreen call state

       Theming & Styling:

       1. Color Scheme:
         - User messages: .blue
         - Assistant messages: .systemGray5 (light gray)
         - Error indicators: .red
         - Success/tools: .green
         - Tint color (global): .orange (in MainTabView)
       2. Typography:
         - Titles: .title2.weight(.semibold)
         - Body text: default
         - Captions: .caption, .caption2
         - Monospaced for JSON: .caption2.monospaced()
       3. Shapes & Styling:
         - Message bubbles: RoundedRectangle (16pt) or BubbleTailShape
         - Input field: RoundedRectangle (20pt), systemGray6 background
         - Tool chips: Capsule shape with status-color backgrounds
         - Call controls: Circles (64pt) with icons
       4. Accessibility:
         - accessibilityLabel on buttons (e.g., "Start/Stop dictation")
         - Semantic HTML-like structure with HStack/VStack
       5. Animations:
         - Typing indicator: repeating easeInOut (0.6s per dot)
         - Audio waveform: scale effect when speaking
         - Tool chip pulse: easeInOut (0.9s) for pending state
         - Page transitions: opacity

       Responsive Layout:
       - Uses GeometryReader for camera preview sizing
       - maxWidth/maxHeight constraints
       - Flexible spacing with Spacer()
       - Safe area consideration with .ignoresSafeArea()

       Key Services Architecture:

       - GeminiService: Singleton, injected into ChatViewModel
       - DictationController: Separate @MainActor class for speech-to-text
       - CallKitManager: Optional, user-enabled feature
       - CameraService: Manages video capture for streaming
       - ChatAttachmentService: Stateless factory for attachment loading
       - ChatSettings: User preferences (read receipts toggle, etc.)
       - LinkMetadataStore: Caches link metadata for previews
       - LiveActivityManager: Dynamic Island activity management

       iMessage and FaceTime UI Patterns - Research Findings

       Based on my comprehensive search of the codebase, here's what I found regarding the iMessage and FaceTime UI
        patterns this project is implementing:

       1. Message Bubble Styling & Alignment

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/ChatMessageBubble.swift

       The app implements authentic iMessage-style bubbles with:
       - Bubble Tail Shape: Custom BubbleTailShape that creates a small triangle "tail" pointing from the bubble
         - User messages (blue) have the tail on the bottom-right
         - Assistant messages (gray) have the tail on the bottom-left
         - Recent refinement (commit 4e8651f): Tail geometry was carefully tuned with proper base positioning and
       offset calculations
       - Rounded Rectangles: 16pt corner radius for standard grouped messages without tails
       - Proper Alignment: Messages align right for user, left for assistant
       - Padding Precision: Specific padding (top: 11pt, bottom: 13pt for tail, 12pt horizontal) matches iMessage's
        exact spacing

       2. Read Receipts & Message Status

       Files:
       - /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/ChatThreadView.swift
       - /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Models/ChatThread.swift

       The app implements a complete message status tracking system:
       - Status Enum: ChatMessageStatus with states: .sending, .sent, .delivered, .read, .failed
       - Display Logic:
         - Only shows status text on the most recent user message at a group boundary
         - Shows: "Sending..." → "Delivered" → "Read" (when toggled on)
         - Shows "Not Delivered" for failed messages with red failure indicator
       - Settings Toggle: showReadReceipts boolean controls visibility (in ChatSettings)
       - Timestamp Display: Messages show time stamps when gap > 5 minutes

       Recent commit (4e8651f) refined the logic to only show status on the most recent user message, preventing
       status clutter.

       3. Typing Indicator

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/TypingIndicatorBubble.swift

       Implements classic iMessage typing animation:
       - Three animated dots in a gray bubble (matching assistant message color)
       - Scale effect: Dots pulse from 0.6x to 1.0x scale
       - Staggered animation: Each dot has a 0.2s delay for ripple effect
       - Duration: 0.6s ease-in-out, repeating forever
       - Appears on left side matching assistant alignment

       4. FaceTime-Like Call Screen UI

       The project implements comprehensive call UI with multiple presentation styles:

       Call View Architecture

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/CallView.swift

       Presentation Styles (enum CallPresentationStyle):
       1. Full Screen - Black gradient background (top-to-bottom)
       2. Translucent Overlay - Live camera feed with semi-transparent black overlay
       3. Picture in Picture - Transparent background for overlay

       Call Controls (Pill-Shaped/Circular)

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/CallControlsView.swift

       FaceTime-like control layout with:
       - Mute/Unmute button - Mic icon, toggles state
       - Audio Route Picker - Using native AVRoutePickerView (system audio selector)
       - Video Toggle - Camera icon, start/stop video
       - Add button - Plus icon for attachments
       - End Call button - Red phone icon (prominent, red background)

       Styling:
       - Circular buttons (64pt diameter)
       - Semi-transparent white backgrounds (0.18 opacity) for control buttons
       - Red background for end call button
       - White icons
       - Caption labels below each button
       - Organized in 2 rows (3 buttons top, 2 bottom)

       Call Status Display

       - Caller Name: "Heard, Chef" at top (title2, semibold, white)
       - Call Duration: Displays when connected
       - Connection Status:
         - "Connecting…" with spinner
         - "Connected"
         - "Reconnecting…"
         - "Connection issue"
       - Animated Dots: 3-dot pulsing animation for connecting state
       - Avatar Circle: 180pt diameter animated circle that scales when speaking

       Picture-in-Picture (PiP) Implementation

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/PiPCallOverlayView.swift

       FaceTime-style floating bar with:
       - Pill-shaped container: RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 16) with ultra-thin material background
       - Constrained layout: Max 420pt width, 56pt height
       - Draggable: Gesture-based positioning with snap points (left, center, right)
       - Compact controls: 28x28 circular buttons in a row
         - Expand button (open chevron)
         - Contact name + status indicator (green/orange dot)
         - Audio route picker
         - Mute toggle
         - Video toggle
         - End call (red)
       - Shadow & Border: Subtle drop shadow and white border for glass effect

       FaceTime Camera Preview

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/FaceTimeCameraPreview.swift

       Handles video streaming background:
       - Integrates with CameraService
       - Shows permission prompt when camera not authorized
       - Streams video frames at 0.2s intervals (5 FPS)
       - Used as background in translucent overlay presentation style

       Audio Controls

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/AudioRoutePickerView.swift

       - Native AVRoutePickerView wrapped in SwiftUI
       - Shows speaker, headphones, and Bluetooth options
       - White tint color for visibility on dark backgrounds

       5. Call State Management

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/ChatViewModel.swift

       CallSessionState structure tracks:
       - isPresented - Whether call UI is shown
       - isListening - Microphone active
       - isSpeaking - Voice output active
       - audioLevel - Real-time audio input level
       - isVideoStreaming - Camera active
       - videoFrameInterval - Capture rate (0.2s default)

       ConnectionState enum:
       - disconnected
       - connecting
       - connected
       - error(String)

       6. Architecture: iMessage vs FaceTime Separation

       Commit f0e7c96 documents the key architectural split:

       ┌──────────┬───────────┬───────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
       │ Feature  │ Protocol  │          Backend          │                     Use Case                      │
       ├──────────┼───────────┼───────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
       │ iMessage │ REST/HTTP │ Gemini 2.5 Flash          │ Text↔Text, Image→Text, Speech→Text (Apple native) │
       ├──────────┼───────────┼───────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
       │ FaceTime │ WebSocket │ Gemini 2.0 Flash Live API │ Speech↔Speech, Image→Speech, Video streaming      │
       └──────────┴───────────┴───────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

       The separation allows:
       - iMessage: Flexible, stateless messaging
       - FaceTime: Real-time bidirectional audio/video streaming

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/ChatMessageBubble.swift

       Context menu with emoji reactions:
       - 👍 ❤️ 😂 😮 😢 😡
       - Stored as comma-separated string
       - Displayed as pill badges below messages
       - Light gray background, small font

       8. Tool Call Chips (Live Status Indicators)

       File: /c/Users/18312/Projects/chef-yes-chef/app/Views/Chat/ChatThreadView.swift

       Shows AI function calls in real-time:
       - Pending state: Orange color, clock icon, pulsing opacity animation
       - Success state: Green color, checkmark icon
       - Error state: Red color, warning icon
       - Capsule-shaped chips: Rounded pill containers
       - Expandable details: Shows function parameters/results

       9. Design References

       - imessage-esque-chat.png - Reference design showing bubble layout, tool chips, and messaging flow
       - stylized-screens.png - Multi-screen layout showing various chat states

       Key Design Principles Observed

       1. Right-Alignment for User, Left for Assistant - Standard iMessage convention
       2. Bubble Tails for Group Boundaries - Only on last message in a sequence
       3. Color Coding - Blue for user, gray for assistant (system gray 5)
       4. Glass Effect - PiP uses .ultraThinMaterial for frosted glass look
       5. Circular Controls - All call buttons are 64pt circles
       6. Minimal Decoration - Clean, Apple-like aesthetic with proper spacing
       7. Real-time Feedback - Animations for typing, speaking, and processing states
       8. Accessibility - Proper contrast, labels, and state indicators

  ⎿  Interrupted · What should Claude do instead?

> 1. getstream (stream-video-swift)

  this is probably the closest to what you're looking for. they have pre-built swiftui components that literally
  mirror the facetime layout.

      the ui: it includes a CallContainer view with a floating, draggable pip that collapses smoothly.

      the controls: it gives you a customizable control bar at the bottom where the mute, speakerphone, and video
  toggles live. you can easily inject a custom + button into their control bar array.

      the texting side: they also maintain a specific open-source repo called swiftui-iMessage-clone which handles
  the texting layout perfectly.

  2. 100ms (hms-roomkit-ios)

  if you want a complete, pre-packaged ui that you can just present, their roomkit is incredibly stable and very
  apple-native.

      the ui: it comes with a built-in grid and a collapsible pip for the local user that handles all the
  edge-snapping math for you.

      the controls: the bottom control bar is fully baked in with mute/speaker/camera. you can use their ui config
  builder to add custom options like your + menu for adding users or triggering actions.

  3. livekit (livekit-ios)

  livekit is a bit more bare-metal than the other two, but their swiftui sdk is rock solid if you want tighter
  control over the design constraints.

      the ui: they provide a VideoView that handles the heavy lifting of the video stream, but you'll have to wrap
  it in your own .gesture(DragGesture()) modifier or custom ZStack to get the exact collapsible pip physics you
  want.

       Perfect! Now I have comprehensive information. Let me provide you with a detailed research report:

       ---
       Research Report: GetStream iOS SDKs for Video Calling and iMessage-Style Chat

       I've completed a thorough research of both the GetStream Video SDK and Chat SDK, along with their example
       projects. Here's a comprehensive breakdown:

       1. STREAM VIDEO SDK (stream-video-swift)

       Overview:
       The StreamVideo iOS SDK provides a complete framework for building video and audio calling applications with
        both low-level WebRTC client and high-level SwiftUI UI components. It supports in-app video calling, audio
       rooms, audio calls, live streaming, screen sharing, picture-in-picture, and call recording.

       Core SwiftUI Components:

       - CallContainer: A high-level composable component that integrates multiple call screens (OutgoingCall,
       IncomingCall, ActiveCall) into one unified interface
         - Automatically handles different call states
         - Takes ViewFactory and CallViewModel as parameters
         - Sets up video grid, call controls, and header components automatically
       - CallControls View: Displays mutable action buttons for call management
         - Default actions: mute/unmute audio, toggle camera, speakerphone, end call
         - Customizable via ViewFactory's makeCallControlsView method
         - Can arrange buttons in HStack with custom spacing
       - Call Video Grid: Adaptive participant layout
         - Renders all active participants using VideoRendererView
         - ParticipantsGridLayout component for flexible grid display
         - Uses SwiftUI's VStack/HStack for layout composition
       - CallViewModel: Central state management object
         - Property: isPictureInPictureEnabled (default: true)
         - Manages call state, participant data, and UI state
         - Directly connected to low-level WebRTC Call object

       Picture-in-Picture (PiP) Implementation:

       - Automatic PiP: When app moves to background, native iOS PiP window appears automatically (iOS 15+)
       - PiP Display: Shows first non-current participant or their screen share
       - Control Options:
         - Control via isPictureInPictureEnabled property on CallViewModel
         - Use enablePictureInPicture view modifier for custom views
         - Apply StreamPictureInPictureAdapter for manual control
       - Camera Access: By default restricted in background; workarounds include Apple entitlement request or iPad
       Stage Manager
       - Floating Behavior: Appears as native iOS PiP overlay with dragging, snapping, and collapsing built-in

       Customization Pattern (ViewFactory):

       The SDK uses a protocol-based ViewFactory pattern for complete UI customization:

       // Key methods to override:
       - makeOutgoingCallView(viewModel:)
       - makeIncomingCallView(viewModel:, callInfo:)
       - makeCallTopView() // Header customization
       - makeCallControlsView() // Bottom control bar
       - makeVideoParticipantsView() // Video grid

       You create a CustomViewFactory class conforming to ViewFactory protocol and pass it to CallContainer. You
       only need to implement methods for components you want to customize.

       Appearance Customization:

       - Appearance class configures all texts, images, fonts, and sounds
       - Supports color theming, custom images for reactions/controls, font sizing
       - Respects system settings (dark mode, dynamic font sizes, accessibility)

       Design Philosophy:
       - Progressive disclosure (basic or advanced usage)
       - Native Swift APIs with type safety
       - Familiar iOS behavior patterns

       ---
       2. STREAM CHAT SDK (StreamChatSwiftUI)

       Overview:
       SwiftUI Chat SDK built on top of the StreamChat framework, supporting iOS 14+. Provides three-tier component
        architecture: Screens (highest level), Stateful Components (with ViewModels), and Stateless Components
       (building blocks).

       Core Chat Components:

       - Channel List Views: Browse and select chat channels
         - Customizable list items with channel metadata
         - CustomChannelListItem support for styling
       - Message List View: Core messaging interface
         - Renders messages with proper alignment and bubbles
         - Supports different message types and layouts
       - Message Bubbles: Core UI elements for messages
         - Bubble Styling: Customizable background color, text color, border radius
         - Alignment: Outgoing messages use .trailing alignment in VStack, incoming use .leading
         - Message Tails: Bubble tail direction depends on message direction (incoming/outgoing)
         - Reactions Display: Built-in emoji reaction display below bubbles
         - Custom Shapes: Override via ChatMessageBubbleView subclassing
       - Message Composer (Input Bar):
         - Four Main Sections:
             i. Leading View: Media picker, command buttons
           ii. Input View: Text entry field with multiline support
           iii. Trailing View: Send button (customizable position)
           iv. Attachment Picker: Images, videos, files, camera input
         - Customization Methods:
             - makeComposerViewModifier() - Style the entire composer
           - makeLeadingComposerView() - Customize media picker
           - makeComposerInputView() - Text input customization
           - makeTrailingComposerView() - Send button customization
         - Features: Keyboard handling, attachment display, cooldown timer, cursor tracking

       Message Layout & Styling:

       - Bubble Alignment (VStack patterns):
         - Outgoing: Use .trailing alignment to push bubble right
         - Incoming: Use .leading alignment with avatar on left
         - HStack wraps avatar + bubble with .bottom alignment
       - Message Container Structure:
         - mainContainer: Holds avatar, spacer, and bubble
         - bubbleThreadMetaContainer: Holds bubble and metadata
         - Components can be repositioned by swapping element order
       - Color Palette:
         - Bubble background colors customizable via ColorPalette
         - Text colors for sent/received messages
         - Supports dynamic theming

       Message Reactions:

       - Display: Emoji reactions shown below message bubble
       - Customization Points:
         - availableReactions property in Images class (part of Appearance)
         - reactionCurrentUserColor - color for user's own reactions
         - reactionOtherUserColor - color for others' reactions
         - makeMessageReactionView() in ViewFactory for complete custom view
       - User Reactions View: Shows who reacted with which emoji
       - Reactions Overlay: Long-press triggers reactions picker with available emoji options

       ViewFactory Pattern for Chat:

       Similar to video SDK, chat uses ViewFactory protocol for customization:
       - makeChannelListDividerItem()
       - makeChannelHeader()
       - makeMessageView()
       - makeMessageComposer()
       - And many more for each UI component

       ---
       3. SwiftUI MESSAGES UI CLONE (GetStream/SwiftUIMessagesUIClone)

       Overview:
       A reference implementation cloning Apple's Messages app in pure SwiftUI, demonstrating best practices for
       chat UI design and animations.

       Architecture & Components:

       - Main Screens:
         - Messages List: Contact list with preview
         - Conversation Screen: Incoming and outgoing messages
       - Message Bubble Components:
         - Custom bubble shapes with rounded corners
         - Animated tails/pointers on bubbles
         - Grouping of consecutive messages from same sender
       - Interactive Animations (9 types):
         - Echo, Cerebration, Confetti, Fireworks, Balloons, Love, Tail, Writing, Combined effects
         - Screen-level animations triggered by message actions
       - Gestures & Interactions:
         - Long-press for context menus and reactions
         - Message scrolling with momentum
         - Pull-to-refresh functionality
         - Tap handling for message selection
       - Layout Patterns:
         - VStack for vertical message flow
         - Custom alignment guides for bubble positioning
         - ZStack for layering effects
         - Spacer elements for responsive padding
       - Message Grouping:
         - Messages from same sender grouped with shared bubble tail style
         - First message shows sender avatar
         - Subsequent messages indent with reduced spacing

       Key Design Patterns Observed:

       1. Bubble Rendering:
         - Custom SwiftUI Shape for bubble with tail
         - Clip modifier to apply shape
         - .foregroundColor() for bubble color
       2. Message Alignment:
         - Outgoing: HStack with message on right
         - Incoming: HStack with avatar on left, message on right
       3. Animation Framework:
         - Transition modifiers for message appearance
         - withAnimation blocks for state changes
         - Custom animation curves for effects
       4. Responsive Design:
         - Uses GeometryReader for sizing bubbles
         - Adaptive padding based on content width
         - Respects safe area insets

       ---
       4. KEY ARCHITECTURAL PATTERNS TO ADOPT

       For FaceTime-Like Call Screen:

       1. Use CallContainer as base, override via ViewFactory
       2. makeCallControlsView for mute/speaker/video/hangup buttons in HStack with 32pt spacing
       3. makeVideoParticipantsView for participant grid using LazyVGrid/adaptive layout
       4. Enable PiP via CallViewModel property, leverage native iOS floating overlay
       5. Override makeCallTopView for custom header (participant info, call duration, etc.)

       For iMessage-Like Chat:

       1. Use MessageList + MessageComposer from StreamChatSwiftUI
       2. Customize message bubbles via ViewFactory's makeMessageView
       3. Implement bubble alignment using VStack with .leading/.trailing
       4. Build composer with four sections: leading (picker), input, trailing (send), attachments
       5. Add reactions via makeMessageReactionView with emoji display
       6. Use ColorPalette for theme consistency

       Design Pattern Summary:
       Both SDKs follow the ViewFactory Protocol Pattern:
       - Define swappable views for each UI component
       - Override only components you need to customize
       - Inject custom ViewFactory into root container
       - Maintain state through ViewModels
       - Use Appearance/ColorPalette for theming

       Excellent! Now I have comprehensive information. Let me compile this research into a detailed report for
       you.

       Research Summary: 100ms RoomKit iOS & LiveKit iOS SDKs

       I've successfully researched both video call UI frameworks being used as reference for your FaceTime-like
       call screen. Here's a comprehensive analysis:

       ---
       1. 100ms RoomKit iOS SDK

       Pre-built UI Components

       HMSPrebuiltView
       - Single production-ready view encapsulating entire video-conferencing experience
       - Instantiated with either a room code or auth token
       - Provides out-of-the-box conferencing and livestreaming UI

       Modular Components
       - HMSPeerLayout: Displays peer tiles in grid layout with automatic participant appearance
       - HMSPeerTile: Individual participant tiles
       - HMSVideoTrackView (SwiftUI) / HMSVideoView (UIKit): Video rendering with Metal support
       - HMSScreenTrackView: Screen sharing content display
       - HMSSampleBufferDisplayView: Alternative UIImageView-based rendering using AVSampleBufferDisplayLayer
       (required for PiP support)

       Grid Layout & Participant Display

       - Reactive Display: Participants automatically appear in HMSPeerLayout as they join
       - Responsive Design: Views adapt to context and room state changes
       - Custom Layout: Developers can design custom meeting screens while reusing HMSPeerLayoutView for grid
       functionality
       - Uses SwiftUI's reactive data binding through @Published property wrappers on models like HMSRoomModel and
       HMSPeerModel

       Bottom Control Bar Design

       - Modular Approach: Developers implement custom control bars combining SwiftUI gestures with room state
       methods
       - Available Methods:
         - toggleMic() - microphone toggle
         - toggleCamera() - camera toggle
         - leaveSession() - async/await based leave functionality
       - Implementation Pattern: Map track to video view for lifecycle management, implement toggle controls for
       muting

       PiP (Picture-in-Picture) Implementation

       Technical Requirements:
       - iOS 15 or later
       - SDK version 0.3.3+
       - com.apple.developer.avfoundation.multitasking-camera-access entitlement

       Key Constraint: HMSVideoView uses Metal rendering, which is unsupported by AVPictureInPictureController.
       Solution requires switching to HMSSampleBufferDisplayView for PiP compatibility.

       Implementation Flow:
       1. Create AVPictureInPictureVideoCallViewController instance
       2. Generate content source via AVPictureInPictureController.ContentSource
       3. Initialize controller with source
       4. Enable automatic PiP or manual activation via startPictureInPicture()

       Resource Management: Disable video view drawing when PiP window closes to conserve resources.

       iOS Gesture Handling: Users can drag PiP window to any corner via tap-and-hold; iOS 15+ supports
       pinch-to-resize.

       UI Customization Builder Pattern

       HMSUITheme Configuration:
       - Central theme object distributed via SwiftUI environment objects
       - Uniform application of colors, typography, and branded insignia across all views
       - All modifications cascade through view hierarchy automatically

       Three Customization Levels:
       1. Minimal: Use HMSPrebuiltView directly for out-of-box functionality
       2. Moderate: Mix prebuilt components like HMSPeerLayout with custom SwiftUI views
       3. Advanced: Build entirely custom interfaces using reactive HMSRoomModel objects through environment system

       State Management Pattern: HMSRoomModel publishes properties like roomState and peerModels for reactive UI
       driving across session lifecycle (notJoined → inMeeting → leftMeeting).

       ---
       2. LiveKit iOS SDK & Components-Swift

       SwiftUI Component Hierarchy

       Core Components (from components-swift library):
       - VideoTrackView: Displays video from participants with configurable trackReference and frame dimensions
       - ForEachParticipant: Iterator for room participants with reactive updates
       - ForEachTrack: Filters and renders specific track types (video/audio/data)
       - ParticipantView: Renders video track of participant using SwiftUIVideoView

       VideoView Component:
       - Critical Constraint: All operations (read/write properties) must be performed from main thread
       - UIKit-based rendering engine (not SwiftUI native)
       - Supports two layout modes: VideoView.LayoutMode enum
       - Has isEnabled property for off-screen optimization (prevents unnecessary CPU usage)
       - Supports frame sizing control

       Call Controls & Connection Management

       Connection Pattern (async/await):
       try await room.connect(url: wsURL, token: token,
           connectOptions: ConnectOptions(enableMicrophone: true))
       try await room.localParticipant.setCamera(enabled: true)

       Delegate-based Architecture:
       - RoomDelegate for lifecycle notifications
       - Key callbacks: didPublishTrack, didSubscribeTrack
       - Enables reactive UI updates when media availability changes
       - Callbacks marshal on SDK's internal thread—developers must use @MainActor or DispatchQueue.main.async for
       UI updates

       Audio Session Management:
       - Automatic AVAudioSession configuration (default behavior)
       - Disableable for CallKit integration scenarios via
       AudioManager.shared.audioSession.isAutomaticConfigurationEnabled = false
       - Audio engine lifecycle control through AudioEngineObserver chains

       PiP & Floating Overlay Implementation

       Current Status:
       - PiP support is in-progress (referenced as GitHub issue #458)
       - A minimal-pip example exists showing custom video rendering approach
       - Uses avSampleBufferDisplayLayer VideoView property with sampleBuffer rendering mode

       Challenges Documented:
       - Renderer invalidation issues with AVPictureInPictureController
       - Orientation switching problems between full-screen and PiP modes (issue #522)
       - Metal rendering limitations (like 100ms) requiring AVSampleBufferDisplayLayer approach

       Proposed Solution:
       - Expose pictureInPictureDisplayLayer property on VideoView
       - This would give access to internal AVSampleBufferDisplayLayer for PiP implementation

       Starting iOS 15: Native Picture-in-Picture adoption is supported for video calls.

       View Layer vs Connection Layer Separation

       Clear Architectural Separation:
       - View Layer: UIKit VideoView class handles video rendering with main-thread constraint
       - Connection Layer: Room object manages WebSocket connections and participant state on SDK's internal thread
       - Audio Layer: AudioManager deliberately decoupled from view layer

       Memory Safety Patterns:
       - Use weak references to SDK-managed objects (participants become invalid on disconnection)
       - Environment object integration for passing room state to child views
       - Conditional rendering based on room.connectionState (disconnected, connected states)

       State Distribution: SDK follows reactive pattern with connection state propagation through delegates,
       requiring explicit marshaling to main thread via @MainActor or DispatchQueue.main.async.

       ---
       3. Comparative Analysis

       Aspect: Pre-built Views
       100ms RoomKit: HMSPrebuiltView (complete)
       LiveKit: Components-swift (modular)
       ────────────────────────────────────────
       Aspect: Grid Layout
       100ms RoomKit: HMSPeerLayout (automatic)
       LiveKit: ForEachParticipant + manual grid
       ────────────────────────────────────────
       Aspect: Video Rendering
       100ms RoomKit: Metal (HMSVideoView) or AVSampleBuffer (PiP)
       LiveKit: UIKit VideoView (always main-thread bound)
       ────────────────────────────────────────
       Aspect: PiP Support
       100ms RoomKit: Built-in, requires HMSSampleBufferDisplayView
       LiveKit: In-progress, requires custom implementation
       ────────────────────────────────────────
       Aspect: Control Bar
       100ms RoomKit: Modular methods (toggleMic, etc.)
       LiveKit: Delegate-based subscriptions
       ────────────────────────────────────────
       Aspect: Theme System
       100ms RoomKit: HMSUITheme environment object
       LiveKit: Manual EnvironmentObject distribution
       ────────────────────────────────────────
       Aspect: Customization Levels
       100ms RoomKit: 3-tier (minimal/moderate/advanced)
       LiveKit: Component-based composition
       ────────────────────────────────────────
       Aspect: Gesture Handling
       100ms RoomKit: Built-in iOS system handling
       LiveKit: Developer-implemented
       ────────────────────────────────────────
       Aspect: Audio Management
       100ms RoomKit: Automatic by default
       LiveKit: Automatic or manual via AudioManager

       ---

  ⎿  Prompt:
       I need you to design an implementation plan for rebuilding the chat screen module of an iOS SwiftUI app
       ("Heard, Chef") to achieve stock Apple iMessage/FaceTime UI parity, with Gemini Live API integration for
       voice/text AI chat.

       Current State

       The app already has a working chat + voice call system:
       - ChatView.swift - Main container with NavigationStack, input bar, message thread, call overlays
       - ChatThreadView.swift - ScrollView + LazyVStack message list with timestamps, tool call chips, typing
       indicator
       - ChatMessageBubble.swift - Blue user / gray assistant bubbles with triangle tail shape, reactions via
       context menu, attachments, link previews
       - ChatInputBar.swift - Plus button, TextField, dictation mic button, send button in HStack
       - CallView.swift - Full-screen call UI with chevron-down dismiss, "Heard, Chef" title, connection status,
       animated avatar circle, CallControlsView
       - CallControlsView.swift - Two-row layout: Row 1 (mute, audio route, video), Row 2 (add, end call red). Each
        button is 64pt circle
       - PiPCallOverlayView.swift - Pill-shaped bar with expand, name+status, audio route, mute, video, end call.
       Draggable with snap to 3 horizontal positions
       - CallPresentationStyle.swift - enum: fullScreen, translucentOverlay, pictureInPicture
       - ChatViewModel.swift (35KB) - State management, WebSocket lifecycle, audio engine capture/playback, tool
       call chips
       - GeminiService.swift (60KB) - WebSocket (audio mode) + REST (text mode), dual model architecture

       The app uses SwiftUI, SwiftData, MVVM, iOS 17+.

       Target: Stock Apple iMessage/FaceTime Look

       The user wants the EXACT stock Apple look. Here's what needs to change:

       iMessage Gaps (Chat Screen)

       1. Input Bar: Apple's iMessage has: camera icon (left), expanding text field with rounded capsule shape and
       "iMessage" placeholder, blue arrow.up.circle.fill send button appears inside the text field on the right
       when there's text. The app currently has plus, textfield, mic, send as separate items in an HStack.
       2. Bubble Tail Shape: Apple uses a curved tail that flows from the bubble corner (like a speech bubble in
       comics). The current implementation uses a straight triangle. The tail should only appear on the LAST
       message in a consecutive group from the same sender.
       3. Message Spacing: Apple uses ~2pt spacing within a group from the same sender, ~8-10pt between groups from
        different senders. The current code uses uniform 12pt spacing.
       4. Tapback Reactions: Apple shows tapback as a small pill that floats overlapping the top-right (for user)
       or top-left (for assistant) corner of the bubble. Current implementation uses context menu buttons and shows
        reactions below the bubble.
       5. Navigation Bar: Apple's Messages shows a small avatar circle + name centered in the nav bar, with video
       call and audio call buttons on the trailing side.
       6. Delivery Indicators: Already good - has sending/delivered/read/failed.
       7. Bubble Corner Radius: Apple uses ~18pt radius. Current uses 16pt.

       FaceTime Gaps (Call Screen)

       1. Call Screen Layout: FaceTime shows the contact name + "FaceTime Audio" subtitle at the very top center.
       Below that is a large avatar/memoji. At the bottom is a rounded rect container holding the control buttons.
       The current layout is close but the controls aren't in a container.
       2. Control Bar: FaceTime Audio call has a single-row layout inside a rounded rect container:
         - Row of 3 equal buttons: Mute, End (red, same size), Speaker
         - For video calls, it's: Mute, End (red), Camera flip
         - The buttons are in a semi-transparent dark container with rounded corners
         - Each button is a filled circle icon, labels below
       3. PiP for Audio Calls: FaceTime doesn't show a floating bar for audio calls - it uses Dynamic Island / Live
        Activity (which the app already has). The current PiP bar is custom and doesn't match Apple's pattern. For
       VIDEO calls, FaceTime shows a small corner-snapping video preview.
       4. Ringing/Connecting State: FaceTime shows "Calling..." with subtle pulsing rings around the avatar. The
       current implementation has ProgressView + text which is fine but could be more polished.
       5. End Call Transition: FaceTime shows "Call Ended" briefly before dismissing.

       Gemini API Layer

       The current GeminiService.swift (60KB) is well-built with:
       - WebSocket for audio mode (gemini-2.5-flash-native-audio-preview)
       - REST for text mode (gemini-2.5-flash)
       - Tool/function calling with 14 tools
       - Audio: PCM 16-bit, 16kHz mono
       - Proper timeout handling, reconnection, state management

       Recommendation: Keep the current custom implementation. The reference repos (swift-gemini-api, pipecat) are
       useful for learning but the app's GeminiService already handles the same WebSocket protocol well. The SDKs
       (GetStream, 100ms, LiveKit) are WebRTC-based for user-to-user calls and are NOT applicable for Gemini AI
       communication - they're UI reference only.

       Reference SDK Patterns Worth Adopting

       From GetStream:
       - ViewFactory pattern for swappable UI components (good for testing/customization)
       - CallContainer that handles all call states in one place

       From the iMessage clone:
       - Custom SwiftUI Shape for curved bubble tails
       - Proper message grouping with alignment guides

       From 100ms:
       - Theme environment object pattern for consistent styling

       Plan Requirements

       Design a phased implementation plan that:
       1. Focuses on UI changes first (user's explicit request)
       2. Keeps the existing GeminiService.swift and ChatViewModel.swift mostly intact
       3. Targets stock Apple iMessage/FaceTime look
       4. Is iterative - can be implemented file by file
       5. Preserves all existing functionality (tool call chips, attachments, link previews, dictation, etc.)
       6. Notes which files to modify vs create new
       7. Includes verification steps

       The plan should be organized by component, not by phase, since the user wants to work through each piece of
       UI.

       ---
       Implementation Plan: iMessage/FaceTime UI Parity for Heard, Chef

       Overview

       This plan rebuilds the chat screen module component-by-component to match stock Apple iMessage and FaceTime
       UI. It preserves the existing ChatViewModel.swift and GeminiService.swift nearly untouched, focusing on the
       view layer. Each component section is self-contained and can be implemented independently.

       ---
       Component 1: Bubble Tail Shape (BubbleTailShape in ChatMessageBubble.swift)

       Problem: The current BubbleTailShape at line 252 of ChatMessageBubble.swift draws a straight triangle below
       the bubble. Apple iMessage uses a curved tail that blends seamlessly from the bottom corner of the bubble,
       flowing outward like a speech-bubble tail in comics. The tail is part of the bubble contour, not a separate
       triangle appended below it.

       What to change: Replace the entire BubbleTailShape struct in
       C:\Users\18312\Projects\chef-yes-chef\app\Views\Chat\ChatMessageBubble.swift (lines 252-281).

       Target design:
       - The bubble body is a rounded rectangle with 18pt corner radius (up from 16pt).
       - On the tail side (bottom-right for user, bottom-left for assistant), the corner radius is 0pt -- the tail
       flows from that corner.
       - The tail is a small curved protrusion (~6pt wide, ~10pt tall) that curves outward and downward from the
       bottom corner using quadratic Bezier curves, then curves back in toward the bubble edge.
       - The path should be a single continuous closed path (not a rounded rect plus a separate triangle).

       Implementation approach:
       func path(in rect: CGRect) -> Path
       Draw the entire bubble as one Path:
       1. Start at top-left corner, arc around to top-right with 18pt radius.
       2. Down the right side. If isUser and this is the tail side:
         - At the bottom-right, instead of rounding, extend the path down and outward using
       addQuadCurve(to:control:) to create the iMessage-style tail.
         - The control point should be offset slightly right and below the corner to create the characteristic
       S-curve.
       3. Across the bottom, back up the left side.
       4. Mirror logic for assistant messages (tail on bottom-left).

       Key measurements from iMessage reference:
       - Tail extends ~6pt horizontally beyond the bubble edge
       - Tail tip is ~4pt below the bubble bottom
       - Two quad curves: one going out, one curving back

       Also update cornerRadius from 16 to 18 throughout bubbleBackground (line 120).

       Verification: Build and confirm that the last message in each sender group shows a curved tail matching
       iMessage screenshots. Non-tail bubbles should show an 18pt rounded rectangle.

       Problem: LazyVStack(spacing: 12) at line 16 of ChatThreadView.swift applies uniform 12pt spacing. Apple
       iMessage uses ~2pt spacing within a same-sender group and ~8pt between different-sender groups. The current
       bottom padding logic (line 78: isGroupEnd ? 8 : 2) partially addresses this but the base 12pt spacing
       overrides it.

       What to change: Modify C:\Users\18312\Projects\chef-yes-chef\app\Views\Chat\ChatThreadView.swift.

       1. Change LazyVStack(spacing: 12) to LazyVStack(spacing: 0) -- manage all spacing via per-message padding.

       let isGroupStart = previousMessage?.role.isUser != message.role.isUser
       3. Replace the current .padding(.bottom, isGroupEnd ? 8 : 2) with:
       .padding(.top, isGroupStart ? 8 : 2)
       .padding(.bottom, 0)
       3. This gives 2pt within a group, 8pt between groups.

● Now I see the full picture. Let me map out what I found — there are clear bugs in both the image attachment flow and
  the audio pipeline that explain why those features are broken.

  ---
  What's Broken & What the Reference SDKs Teach Us

  1. Image Attachments (broken)

  The bug is in ChatView.swift:87-91:
  private func handleSelectedItemChange() {
      guard selectedItem != nil else { return }
      Task {
          selectedItem = nil  // ← Just clears it! Never loads the image data
      }
  }

  The PhotosPickerItem gets selected, then immediately discarded without extracting its data into a ChatAttachment. The
  REST API path (sendPhotoREST / sendTextWithPhotoREST) is actually fine — it properly base64-encodes and sends to
  Gemini. The pipeline is just never fed.

  2. Calling (completely broken) — Two critical audio bugs

  Bug A: Audio Capture sends wrong sample rate

  ChatViewModel.swift:443-446 — The capture tap uses inputNode.outputFormat(forBus: 0) which is the device's native rate
   (44.1kHz or 48kHz). Then convertToPCM16() just clips float→Int16 without resampling. But the WebSocket declares
  audio/pcm;rate=16000. So Gemini receives 48kHz audio labeled as 16kHz — it sounds like chipmunks or garbage.

  What GetStream/LiveKit/100ms do: They all use AVAudioConverter to resample from the device's native format down to the
   target format before sending. The pattern from swift-gemini-api:

  let inputFormat = inputNode.outputFormat(forBus: 0)
  let targetFormat = AVAudioFormat(commonFormat: .pcmFormatInt16, sampleRate: 16000, channels: 1, interleaved: false)!
  let converter = AVAudioConverter(from: inputFormat, to: targetFormat)!

  // In the tap callback:
  let ratio = 16000.0 / inputFormat.sampleRate
  let capacity = UInt32(Double(buffer.frameLength) * ratio)
  let convertedBuffer = AVAudioPCMBuffer(pcmFormat: targetFormat, frameCapacity: capacity)!
  converter.convert(to: convertedBuffer, error: nil) { _, outStatus in
      outStatus.pointee = .haveData
      return buffer
  }
  // Now send convertedBuffer data

  Bug B: Playback engine configured at wrong rate

  ChatViewModel.swift:538 — Playback format is set to 16kHz:
  let format = AVAudioFormat(commonFormat: .pcmFormatInt16, sampleRate: 16_000, channels: 1, interleaved: false)

  But the Gemini Live API returns audio at 24kHz (per the API spec). Playing 24kHz audio at 16kHz makes everything sound
   slow and distorted.

  What the reference SDKs do: They match the playback format to the server's output format. For Gemini Live, that's
  24000 Hz.

  3. Speakerphone Toggle

  This part actually looks correct:
  - preferSpeaker() calls session.overrideOutputAudioPort(.speaker) ✓
  - AudioRoutePickerView wraps the native AVRoutePickerView ✓
  - AVAudioSession is configured with .defaultToSpeaker, .allowBluetoothHFP ✓

  The pattern matches exactly what GetStream and 100ms do. No changes needed — once the audio pipeline is fixed, speaker
   routing should work.

  4. Mute

  Also looks correct:
  - toggleMute() stops/starts the audio capture engine ✓
  - CallKit's onMuteChanged callback syncs mute state ✓
  - This matches the guard !isMuted else { return } pattern from swift-gemini-api

  One refinement from GetStream: Instead of fully stopping the engine, just stop sending packets (cheaper, faster
  toggle):
  // Current: stops entire AVAudioEngine (expensive)
  // Better: keep engine running, flag to skip sending
  func toggleMute() {
      isMuted.toggle()
      // In processAudioBuffer: guard !isMuted else { return }
  }

  5. Collapse/Expand (Dismiss Call Screen)

  The presentation style architecture is solid:
  - fullScreen → .fullScreenCover ✓
  - translucentOverlay → ZStack overlay ✓
  - pictureInPicture → draggable PiP bar ✓

  What 100ms/GetStream do differently: When collapsing from fullscreen to background, they don't use a custom PiP bar
  for audio calls. They rely entirely on the system's Dynamic Island / Live Activity — which you already have via
  LiveActivityManager. The PiP bar is only for video calls showing a small corner-snapping video preview.

  So the collapse flow should be:
  - Audio call: Dismiss fullscreen → Dynamic Island takes over → tap Dynamic Island → returns to fullscreen
  - Video call: Dismiss fullscreen → corner-snapping video PiP overlay (future)

  6. Connection Lifecycle

  The WebSocket lifecycle has a subtle issue. In geminiServiceDidDisconnect, the ViewModel immediately calls
  connect(mode: .audio) to reconnect:

  func geminiServiceDidDisconnect(_ service: GeminiService) {
      ...
      if callState.isPresented {
          pauseCallTimer()
          pendingVoiceStart = true
          connect(mode: .audio)  // ← immediate reconnect
      }
  }

  What GetStream/LiveKit do: They use exponential backoff for reconnection (1s, 2s, 4s...) with a max retry count.
  Immediate reconnection can cause a tight loop if the server keeps rejecting.
